      <p>
       <b>
        Benin
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <small>
         <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">
          US
         </a>
         :
        </small>
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          , -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         bǝ-
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          NEEN
         </span>
        </i>
       </a>
       or -
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          NIN
         </span>
        </i>
       </a>
       ;
       <span class="nowrap">
        <small>
         <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">
          UK
         </a>
         :
        </small>
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'b' in 'buy'">
            b
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">
            ɛ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">
            iː
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         beh-
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          NEEN
         </span>
        </i>
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         Bénin
        </span>
       </i>
       <small>
        pronounced
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">
         [benɛ̃]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Benin
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         République du Bénin
        </span>
       </i>
       ) and formerly
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Dahomey" title="Republic of Dahomey">
         Dahomey
        </a>
       </b>
       , is a country in
       <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">
        West Africa
       </a>
       . It is bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">
        Togo
       </a>
       to the west,
       <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
        Nigeria
       </a>
       to the east, and
       <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">
        Burkina Faso
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">
        Niger
       </a>
       to the north. The majority of its population lives on the small southern coastline of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bight_of_Benin" title="Bight of Benin">
        Bight of Benin
       </a>
       , part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">
        Gulf of Guinea
       </a>
       in the northernmost tropical portion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HughesHughes1992_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HughesHughes1992-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The capital of Benin is
       <a href="/wiki/Porto-Novo" title="Porto-Novo">
        Porto-Novo
       </a>
       , but the
       <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_government" title="Seat of government">
        seat of government
       </a>
       is in
       <a href="/wiki/Cotonou" title="Cotonou">
        Cotonou
       </a>
       , the country's largest city and economic capital. Benin covers an area of 114,763 square kilometers
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AS2010_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AS2010-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and its population in 2016 was estimated to be approximately 10.87 million
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . Benin is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">
        tropical
       </a>
       nation, highly dependent on
       <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">
        agriculture
       </a>
       , with substantial employment and income arising from
       <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">
        subsistence farming
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       of Benin is
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       . However, indigenous languages such as
       <a href="/wiki/Fon_language" title="Fon language">
        Fon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">
        Yoruba
       </a>
       are commonly spoken. The largest religious group in Benin is
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       , followed closely by
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vodun" title="Vodun">
        Vodun
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
        Protestantism
       </a>
       . Benin is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
        African Union
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">
        Organisation of Islamic Cooperation
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Peace_and_Cooperation_Zone" title="South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone">
        South Atlantic Peace and Cooperation Zone
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        La Francophonie
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel-Saharan_States" title="Community of Sahel-Saharan States">
        Community of Sahel-Saharan States
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/African_Petroleum_Producers_Association" title="African Petroleum Producers Association">
        African Petroleum Producers Association
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Niger_Basin_Authority" title="Niger Basin Authority">
        Niger Basin Authority
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 17th to the 19th century, the main political entities in the area were the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dahomey" title="Kingdom of Dahomey">
        Kingdom of Dahomey
       </a>
       , along with the city-state of
       <a href="/wiki/Porto-Novo" title="Porto-Novo">
        Porto-Novo
       </a>
       , and a large area with many different tribes to the north. This region was referred to as the
       <a href="/wiki/Slave_Coast_of_West_Africa" title="Slave Coast of West Africa">
        Slave Coast
       </a>
       from as early as the 17th century due to the large number of slaves shipped to the New World during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Trans-Atlantic slave trade">
        Trans-Atlantic slave trade
       </a>
       . After slavery was abolished, France took over the country and renamed it as
       <a href="/wiki/French_Dahomey" title="French Dahomey">
        French Dahomey
       </a>
       . In 1960, Dahomey gained full independence from France. It has had a tumultuous history since then, with many different democratic governments, military coups, and military governments.
      </p>
      <p>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">
        Marxist–Leninist
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">
        state
       </a>
       called the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Benin" title="People's Republic of Benin">
        People's Republic of Benin
       </a>
       existed between 1975 and 1990. In 1991, it was replaced by the current
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">
        multi-party
       </a>
       Republic of Benin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ibp_Usa_p85_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ibp_Usa_p85-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       During the colonial period and at independence, the country was
       <a href="/wiki/Geographical_renaming" title="Geographical renaming">
        known as
       </a>
       <b>
        Dahomey
       </b>
       . On 30 November 1975 it was renamed to
       <b>
        Benin
       </b>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeaRowe2001_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LeaRowe2001-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       after the body of water on which the country lies—the
       <a href="/wiki/Bight_of_Benin" title="Bight of Benin">
        Bight of Benin
       </a>
       . This had been named by Europeans after the
       <a href="/wiki/Benin_Empire" title="Benin Empire">
        Benin Empire
       </a>
       (present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
        Nigeria
       </a>
       ). The country of Benin has no connection to
       <a href="/wiki/Benin_City" title="Benin City">
        Benin City
       </a>
       in modern Nigeria, nor to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benin_bronzes" title="Benin bronzes">
        Benin bronzes
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Benin_Empire" title="Benin Empire">
        form "Benin"
       </a>
       is the result of a Portuguese corruption of the city of Ubinu (now Benin City).
      </p>
      <p>
       The new name, Benin, was chosen for its neutrality. Dahomey was the name of the former
       <a href="/wiki/Dahomey" title="Dahomey">
        Kingdom of Dahomey
       </a>
       , which was limited to most of the southern third of the present country and therefore did not represent
       <a href="/wiki/Porto-Novo" title="Porto-Novo">
        Porto-Novo
       </a>
       (a rival state in the south), the northwestern sector
       <a href="/wiki/Atakora_Department" title="Atakora Department">
        Atakora
       </a>
       , nor the kingdom of
       <a href="/wiki/Borgu" title="Borgu">
        Borgu
       </a>
       , which covered the northeastern third.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith2008_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Smith2008-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks vcard" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%">

       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Benin" title="History of Benin">
        History of Benin
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Precolonial_history">
        Precolonial history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Precolonial history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The current country of Benin combines three areas which had distinctly different political systems and ethnicities prior to French colonial control. Before 1700, there were a few important city states along the coast (primarily of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aja_people" title="Aja people">
        Aja
       </a>
       ethnic group, but also including
       <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">
        Yoruba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gbe_languages" title="Gbe languages">
        Gbe
       </a>
       peoples) and a mass of tribal regions inland (composed of Bariba, Mahi, Gedevi, and Kabye peoples). The
       <a href="/wiki/Oyo_Empire" title="Oyo Empire">
        Oyo Empire
       </a>
       , located primarily to the east of modern Benin, was the most significant large-scale military force in the region. It regularly conducted raids and exacted tribute from the coastal kingdoms and the tribal regions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bay-1998_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bay-1998-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The situation changed in the 1600s and early 1700s as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Dahomey" title="Kingdom of Dahomey">
        Kingdom of Dahomey
       </a>
       , comprised mostly of
       <a href="/wiki/Fon_people" title="Fon people">
        Fon people
       </a>
       , was founded on the
       <a href="/wiki/Abomey" title="Abomey">
        Abomey
       </a>
       plateau and began taking over areas along the coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 1727, king
       <a href="/wiki/Agaja" title="Agaja">
        Agaja
       </a>
       of the Kingdom of Dahomey had conquered the coastal cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Allada" title="Allada">
        Allada
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ouidah" title="Ouidah">
        Whydah
       </a>
       , but it had become a tributary of the Oyo empire and did not directly attack the Oyo allied city-state of
       <a href="/wiki/Porto-Novo" title="Porto-Novo">
        Porto-Novo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Law-1986_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Law-1986-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rise of the kingdom of Dahomey, the rivalry between the kingdom and the city of Porto-Novo, and the continued tribal politics of the northern region, persisted into the colonial and post-colonial periods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Dahomey" title="Dahomey">
        Dahomey Kingdom
       </a>
       was known for its culture and traditions. Young boys were often apprenticed to older soldiers, and taught the kingdom's military customs until they were old enough to join the army.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harms2002_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Harms2002-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dahomey was also famous for instituting an elite female soldier corps, called
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahosi" title="Ahosi">
        Ahosi
       </a>
       , i.e. the king's wives, or Mino, "our mothers" in the Fon language
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fongbe" title="Fongbe">
        Fongbe
       </a>
       , and known by many Europeans as the Dahomean
       <a href="/wiki/Amazons" title="Amazons">
        Amazons
       </a>
       . This emphasis on military preparation and achievement earned Dahomey the nickname of "black
       <a href="/wiki/Sparta" title="Sparta">
        Sparta
       </a>
       " from European observers and 19th-century explorers such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Richard_Burton" title="Sir Richard Burton">
        Sir Richard Burton
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alpern1998_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Alpern1998-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_Empire">
        Portuguese Empire
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Portuguese Empire">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="371" data-file-width="760" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg/220px-Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg/330px-Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg/440px-Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kingdom_of_Dahomy-1793.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the Kingdom of Dahomey, 1793
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The kings of Dahomey sold their war captives into
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
        transatlantic slavery
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They also had a practice of killing war captives in a ceremony known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Annual_Customs_of_Dahomey" title="Annual Customs of Dahomey">
        Annual Customs
       </a>
       . By about 1750, the King of Dahomey was earning an estimated £250,000 per year by selling African captives to European slave-traders.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dahomey_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dahomey-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Though the leaders of Dahomey appeared initially to have resisted the slave trade, it flourished in the region of Dahomey for almost three hundred years, beginning in 1472 with a trade agreement with
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       merchants. The area was named "the Slave Coast" because of the flourishing trade. Court protocols, which demanded that a portion of war captives from the kingdom's many battles be decapitated, decreased the number of enslaved people exported from the area. The number went from 102,000 people per decade in the 1780s to 24,000 per decade by the 1860s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head,_going_to_war-1793.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="663" data-file-width="760" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head%2C_going_to_war-1793.jpg/220px-Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head%2C_going_to_war-1793.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head%2C_going_to_war-1793.jpg/330px-Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head%2C_going_to_war-1793.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head%2C_going_to_war-1793.jpg/440px-Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head%2C_going_to_war-1793.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Armed_women_with_the_King_at_their_head,_going_to_war-1793.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Dahomey_Amazons" title="Dahomey Amazons">
          Dahomey Amazons
         </a>
         with the King at their head, going to war, 1793
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The decline was partly due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">
        banning
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Trans-Atlantic slave trade">
        trans-Atlantic slave trade
       </a>
       by Britain and the United States in 1808, followed by other countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dahomey_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-dahomey-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This decline continued until 1885, when the last slave ship departed from the coast of the present-day Benin Republic bound for
       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
        Brazil
       </a>
       in South America, that had yet to abolish slavery.
      </p>
      <p>
       The capital's name
       <a href="/wiki/Porto-Novo" title="Porto-Novo">
        Porto-Novo
       </a>
       is of Portuguese origin, meaning "New Port". It was originally developed as a port for the slave trade.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Colonial_period_.281900_until_1958.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period_(1900_until_1958)">
        Colonial period (1900 until 1958)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Colonial period (1900 until 1958)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       By the middle of the nineteenth century, Dahomey had begun to weaken and lose its status as the regional power. This enabled the French to take over the area in 1892. In 1899, the French included the land called
       <a href="/wiki/French_Dahomey" title="French Dahomey">
        French Dahomey
       </a>
       within the larger
       <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">
        French West Africa
       </a>
       colonial region.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1958, France granted autonomy to the
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Dahomey" title="Republic of Dahomey">
        Republic of Dahomey
       </a>
       , and full independence on 1 August 1960. The president who led the country to independence was
       <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Maga" title="Hubert Maga">
        Hubert Maga
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stokes2009_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stokes2009-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Araujo2010_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Araujo2010-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-colonial_period">
        Post-colonial period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post-colonial period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       For the next twelve years after 1960, ethnic strife contributed to a period of turbulence. There were several coups and regime changes, with the figures of
       <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Maga" title="Hubert Maga">
        Hubert Maga
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sourou_Migan_Apithy" title="Sourou Migan Apithy">
        Sourou Apithy
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justin_Ahomadegb%C3%A9" title="Justin Ahomadegbé">
        Justin Ahomadegbé
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emile_Derlin_Zinsou" title="Emile Derlin Zinsou">
        Emile Derlin Zinsou
       </a>
       dominating; the first three each represented a different area and ethnicity of the country. These three agreed to form a
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Council_(Benin)" title="Presidential Council (Benin)">
        Presidential Council
       </a>
       after violence marred the 1970 elections.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Benin_(1975-1990).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Flag_of_Benin_%281975-1990%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Benin_%281975-1990%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Flag_of_Benin_%281975-1990%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Benin_%281975-1990%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Flag_of_Benin_%281975-1990%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Benin_%281975-1990%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Benin_(1975-1990).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The flag of the
         <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Benin" title="People's Republic of Benin">
          People's Republic of Benin
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 7 May 1972, Maga ceded power to Ahomadegbé. On 26 October 1972, Lt. Col.
       <a href="/wiki/Mathieu_K%C3%A9r%C3%A9kou" title="Mathieu Kérékou">
        Mathieu Kérékou
       </a>
       overthrew the ruling triumvirate, becoming president and stating that the country would not "burden itself by copying foreign
       <a href="/wiki/Ideology" title="Ideology">
        ideology
       </a>
       , and wants neither Capitalism, Communism, nor Socialism". On 30 November 1974 however, he announced that the country was officially
       <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">
        Marxist
       </a>
       , under control of the Military Council of the Revolution (CNR), which nationalized the petroleum industry and banks. On 30 November 1975, he renamed the country to the
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Benin" title="People's Republic of Benin">
         People's Republic of Benin
        </a>
       </b>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dickovick2012_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dickovick2012-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HoungnikpoDecalo2012_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HoungnikpoDecalo2012-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The CNR was dissolved in 1979, and Kérékou arranged
       <a href="/wiki/Show_election" title="Show election">
        show elections
       </a>
       in which he was the only allowed candidate. Establishing relations with
       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
        China
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">
        North Korea
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Socialist_People%27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" title="Great Socialist People's Libyan Arab Jamahiriya">
        Libya
       </a>
       , he put nearly all businesses and economic activities under state control, causing foreign investment in Benin to dry up.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kneib_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kneib-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Kérékou attempted to reorganize education, pushing his own aphorisms such as "Poverty is not a fatality", resulting in a mass
       <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">
        exodus
       </a>
       of teachers, along with numerous other professionals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kneib_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-kneib-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The regime financed itself by contracting to take nuclear waste, first from the Soviet Union and later from France.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kneib_26-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-kneib-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1980, Kérékou converted to
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       and changed his first name to Ahmed. He changed his name back after claiming to be a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Born-again_Christian" title="Born-again Christian">
        born-again Christian
       </a>
       . In 1989, riots broke out when the regime did not have enough money to pay its army. The banking system collapsed. Eventually Kérékou renounced
       <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">
        Marxism
       </a>
       , and a convention forced Kérékou to release political prisoners and arrange elections.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kneib_26-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-kneib-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxism-Leninism" title="Marxism-Leninism">
        Marxism-Leninism
       </a>
       was abolished as the nation's form of government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The country's name was officially changed to the
       <i>
        Republic of Benin
       </i>
       on 1 March 1990, after the newly formed government's
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">
        constitution
       </a>
       was completed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1500" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg/220px-BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg/330px-BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg/440px-BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BoniYayi_inauguration2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Boni_Yayi" title="Thomas Boni Yayi">
          Yayi Boni
         </a>
         's 2006 presidential inauguration
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In a 1991 election, Kérékou lost to
       <a href="/wiki/Nic%C3%A9phore_Soglo" title="Nicéphore Soglo">
        Nicéphore Soglo
       </a>
       . Kérékou returned to power after winning the 1996 vote. In 2001, a closely fought election resulted in Kérékou winning another term, after which his opponents claimed election irregularities.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1999, Kérékou issued a national apology for the substantial role that Africans had played in the Atlantic slave trade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Kérékou and former president Soglo did not run in the 2006 elections, as both were barred by the constitution's restrictions on age and total terms of candidates.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 5 March 2006,
       <a href="/wiki/Beninese_presidential_election,_2006" title="Beninese presidential election, 2006">
        an election
       </a>
       was held that was considered free and fair. It resulted in a
       <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">
        runoff
       </a>
       between
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Boni_Yayi" title="Thomas Boni Yayi">
        Yayi Boni
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Adrien_Houngb%C3%A9dji" title="Adrien Houngbédji">
        Adrien Houngbédji
       </a>
       . The runoff election was held on 19 March and was won by Boni, who assumed office on 6 April. The success of the fair multi-party elections in Benin won praise internationally. Boni was
       <a href="/wiki/Beninese_presidential_election,_2011" title="Beninese presidential election, 2011">
        reelected in 2011
       </a>
       , taking 53.18% of the vote in the first round—enough to avoid a runoff election. He was the first president to win an election without a runoff since the restoration of democracy in 1991.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Beninese_presidential_election,_2016" title="Beninese presidential election, 2016">
        March 2016 presidential elections
       </a>
       , in which Boni Yayi was barred by the constitution from running for a third term, businessman
       <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Talon" title="Patrice Talon">
        Patrice Talon
       </a>
       won the second round with 65.37% of the vote, defeating investment banker and former Prime Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Zinsou" title="Lionel Zinsou">
        Lionel Zinsou
       </a>
       . Talon was sworn in on 6 April 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Speaking on the same day that the Constitutional Court confirmed the results, Talon said that he would "first and foremost tackle constitutional reform", discussing his plan to limit presidents to a single term of five years in order to combat "complacency". He also said that he planned to slash the size of the government from 28 to 16 members.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Benin" title="Politics of Benin">
        Politics of Benin
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Benin's politics take place in a framework of a
       <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">
        presidential
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">
        republic
       </a>
       , in which the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_Benin" title="President of Benin">
        President of Benin
       </a>
       is both
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       , within a
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">
        multi-party system
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">
        Executive power
       </a>
       is exercised by the government.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">
        Legislative power
       </a>
       is vested in both the government and the legislature. The
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
        judiciary
       </a>
       is independent of the executive and the legislature. The political system is derived from the 1990
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Benin" title="Constitution of Benin">
        Constitution of Benin
       </a>
       and the subsequent transition to
       <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">
        democracy
       </a>
       in 1991.
      </p>
      <p>
       Benin scored highly in the 2013
       <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">
        Ibrahim Index of African Governance
       </a>
       , which comprehensively measures the state of governance across the continent. Benin was ranked 18th out of 52 African countries, and scored best in the categories of Safety &amp; Rule of Law and Participation &amp; Human Rights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IIAG_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IIAG-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In its 2007 Worldwide Press Freedom Index,
       <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">
        Reporters Without Borders
       </a>
       ranked Benin 53rd out of 169 countries.
      </p>
      <p>
       Benin has been rated equal-88th out of 159 countries in a 2005 analysis of police, business and political corruption.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Departments_and_communes">
        Departments and communes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Departments and communes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Benin" title="Departments of Benin">
        Departments of Benin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Benin" title="Communes of Benin">
        Communes of Benin
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <div class="noresize">
         <map name="ImageMap_1_1203925653">

         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="995" data-file-width="500" height="438" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Benin_departments_named.png/220px-Benin_departments_named.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Benin_departments_named.png/330px-Benin_departments_named.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Benin_departments_named.png/440px-Benin_departments_named.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_1_1203925653" width="220"/>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benin_departments_named.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Departments of Benin.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Benin is divided into twelve
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_(subnational_entity)" title="Department (subnational entity)">
        departments
       </a>
       (French:
       <i>
        départements
       </i>
       ) which, in turn, are subdivided into 77
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commune_(subnational_entity)" title="Commune (subnational entity)">
        communes
       </a>
       . In 1999, the previous six departments were each split into two halves, forming the current twelve. The six new departments were assigned official capitals in 2008.
      </p>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benin&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demography_of_Benin" title="Demography of Benin">
        Demography of Benin
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Benin" title="Languages of Benin">
        Languages of Benin
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:K640_b_160.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/K640_b_160.jpg/220px-K640_b_160.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/K640_b_160.jpg/330px-K640_b_160.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/K640_b_160.jpg/440px-K640_b_160.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:K640_b_160.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Children in Benin
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The majority of Benin's population lives in the south. The population is young, with a
       <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">
        life expectancy
       </a>
       of 62 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       About 42 African ethnic groups live in this country; these various groups settled in Benin at different times and also migrated within the country. Ethnic groups include the
       <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">
        Yoruba
       </a>
       in the southeast (migrated from Nigeria in the 12th century); the
       <a href="/wiki/Dendi_people" title="Dendi people">
        Dendi
       </a>
       in the north-central area (who came from Mali in the 16th century); the
       <a href="/wiki/Bariba_people" title="Bariba people">
        Bariba
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">
        Fula
       </a>
       in the northeast; the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betammaribe" title="Betammaribe">
        Betammaribe
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Somba_people" title="Somba people">
        Somba
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Atacora_Range&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Atacora Range (page does not exist)">
        Atacora Range
       </a>
       ; the
       <a href="/wiki/Fon_people" title="Fon people">
        Fon
       </a>
       in the area around
       <a href="/wiki/Abomey" title="Abomey">
        Abomey
       </a>
       in the South Central and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mina_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mina people (page does not exist)">
        Mina
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xueda_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xueda people (page does not exist)">
        Xueda
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Aja_people" title="Aja people">
        Aja
       </a>
       (who came from Togo) on the coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bn-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Recent migrations have brought other African nationals to Benin that include Nigerians, Togolese, and Malians. The foreign community also includes many Lebanese and Indians involved in trade and commerce. The personnel of the many European embassies and foreign aid missions and of nongovernmental organizations and various missionary groups account for a large part of the
       <span style="white-space:nowrap">
        5
        <span style="margin-left:0.25em">
         500
        </span>
       </span>
       European population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_38-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bn-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A small part of the European population consists of Beninese citizens of
       <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">
        French ancestry
       </a>
       , whose ancestors ruled Benin and left after independence.
      </p>
